how can we check to see the differences in my test db on neon and the productionn db on neon?

You can compare Neon test vs Neon prod at three levels (fast → thorough). Here’s the clean playbook ✅🧪⚙️

1) Fast sanity check (Neon Console)
Use this when you just want “are schemas drifting?”

In Neon (for each project/environment)
Open Neon Console → SQL Editor

Run these:

List schemas

SELECT schema_name
FROM information_schema.schemata
ORDER BY schema_name;
List tables (public)

SELECT table_name
FROM information_schema.tables
WHERE table_schema = 'public' AND table_type='BASE TABLE'
ORDER BY table_name;
List columns per table

SELECT table_name, column_name, data_type, is_nullable, column_default
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_schema='public'
ORDER BY table_name, ordinal_position;
Compare output side-by-side (copy/paste to a diff tool).

2) Correct way (schema diff via pg_dump --schema-only)
This is the best-practice method because it compares actual DDL (types, constraints, indexes, defaults).

Step A — get connection strings
Neon → Connection Details

Grab both DATABASE URLs:

TEST_DATABASE_URL

PROD_DATABASE_URL

Step B — dump schemas
Run locally (or in your terminal in the project) 👇

pg_dump "$TEST_DATABASE_URL" --schema-only --no-owner --no-privileges > test_schema.sql
pg_dump "$PROD_DATABASE_URL" --schema-only --no-owner --no-privileges > prod_schema.sql
Step C — diff them
diff -u prod_schema.sql test_schema.sql | less
(or use VS Code “Compare Active File With…”)

This will show:

missing tables

missing columns

changed types/defaults

missing indexes

constraints drifting

enum differences

3) Best-in-class (migration + drift detection tooling)
If you want this automated in CI:

Option A: migra (simple and excellent for Postgres diffs)
pip install migra
migra "$PROD_DATABASE_URL" "$TEST_DATABASE_URL" > drift.sql
Outputs SQL needed to transform prod → test (or vice versa depending order).

Great for drift detection.

Option B: pgAdmin / DataGrip diff
DataGrip can compare schemas visually (tables, columns, FK, indexes).
Good if you want a UI.

What you should compare (minimum checklist)
Even if tables match, these commonly drift:

✅ Extensions

SELECT extname FROM pg_extension ORDER BY extname;
✅ Enums

SELECT t.typname AS enum_name, e.enumlabel AS enum_value, e.enumsortorder
FROM pg_type t
JOIN pg_enum e ON t.oid = e.enumtypid
JOIN pg_namespace n ON n.oid = t.typnamespace
WHERE n.nspname = 'public'
ORDER BY enum_name, enumsortorder;
✅ Indexes

SELECT tablename, indexname, indexdef
FROM pg_indexes
WHERE schemaname='public'
ORDER BY tablename, indexname;
✅ Constraints

SELECT conrelid::regclass AS table_name, conname, pg_get_constraintdef(oid) AS def
FROM pg_constraint
WHERE connamespace = 'public'::regnamespace
ORDER BY table_name::text, conname;
Neon-specific gotchas (important)
Neon uses branches. Your “test” may literally be a different branch of the same project.

Make sure you’re comparing the right:

Project

Branch

Database name (often neondb)

Role/user

My recommendation for you (PureTask)
Do Method #2 as the baseline (pg_dump schema-only).
Then run the enum + index queries to catch the sneaky drift.

If you tell me how you’re separating environments in Neon:

separate projects? or branches?
…and what OS you’re on (Windows vs Mac/Linux), I’ll give you the exact terminal commands and where to paste the URLs (safe patterns, .env handling, etc.).


speerate branches

Great — separate branches in Neon makes this cleaner. ✅ Here’s the exact, reliable way to diff schema drift between a test branch and prod branch.

1) Get the two connection strings (per branch)
In Neon Console:

Open your Project

Click the prod branch → Connection details → copy the connection string (or endpoint host + db/user)

Click the test branch → Connection details → copy the connection string

Important: confirm each branch’s endpoint hostname is different (Neon branch endpoints usually differ).

You’ll end up with:

PROD_DATABASE_URL=postgres://...@<prod-host>/<db>?sslmode=require

TEST_DATABASE_URL=postgres://...@<test-host>/<db>?sslmode=require

2) Best practice: dump schema-only from each branch and diff
Run from your terminal (Cursor terminal is fine).

macOS / Linux / WSL
pg_dump "$PROD_DATABASE_URL" --schema-only --no-owner --no-privileges > prod_schema.sql
pg_dump "$TEST_DATABASE_URL" --schema-only --no-owner --no-privileges > test_schema.sql

diff -u prod_schema.sql test_schema.sql | less
Windows PowerShell (common gotcha: quotes)
pg_dump "$env:PROD_DATABASE_URL" --schema-only --no-owner --no-privileges | Out-File -Encoding utf8 prod_schema.sql
pg_dump "$env:TEST_DATABASE_URL" --schema-only --no-owner --no-privileges | Out-File -Encoding utf8 test_schema.sql

git diff --no-index prod_schema.sql test_schema.sql
✅ This catches: tables, columns, enums, constraints, indexes, defaults.

3) If you want a “drift SQL patch” (super useful): migra
This generates SQL to reconcile one branch to the other.

pip install migra
migra "$PROD_DATABASE_URL" "$TEST_DATABASE_URL" > drift_prod_to_test.sql
migra "$TEST_DATABASE_URL" "$PROD_DATABASE_URL" > drift_test_to_prod.sql
drift_test_to_prod.sql is often what you want if prod is truth and test drifted.

Or vice versa.

4) Neon-branch-aware “quick checks” (inside SQL Editor)
Run these on both branches and compare output:

Extensions
SELECT extname FROM pg_extension ORDER BY extname;
Enums
SELECT t.typname AS enum_name, e.enumlabel AS enum_value, e.enumsortorder
FROM pg_type t
JOIN pg_enum e ON t.oid = e.enumtypid
JOIN pg_namespace n ON n.oid = t.typnamespace
WHERE n.nspname = 'public'
ORDER BY enum_name, enumsortorder;
Tables
SELECT table_name
FROM information_schema.tables
WHERE table_schema='public' AND table_type='BASE TABLE'
ORDER BY table_name;
Indexes
SELECT tablename, indexname, indexdef
FROM pg_indexes
WHERE schemaname='public'
ORDER BY tablename, indexname;
5) The “real” production-safe workflow (recommended) 🧱
Because you’re using branches, do this:

Treat prod branch as source of truth

Always run migrations on test branch first

If clean, promote/merge or re-run migrations on prod branch

Keep a “schema snapshot” file in git:

db/schema.prod.sql (generated by pg_dump schema-only)

Optional: db/schema.test.sql

That way, drift becomes obvious in PRs.

6) Common Neon branch mistake (watch this)
Even on separate branches, you can accidentally point both envs to the same branch if:

.env has only one DATABASE_URL

you use pooled endpoint vs direct endpoint inconsistently

✅ Quick verification:
Run on each branch:

SELECT current_database(), current_user, inet_server_addr(), inet_server_port();
If these are identical across “test” and “prod”, you’re not actually hitting different endpoints.

If you tell me your OS (Windows PowerShell vs Mac/Linux) and whether you’re using pooled or direct Neon connection strings, I’ll give you the exact copy-paste commands with zero footguns.


can u explain the mistake u described in more detail

Yes — this is an important one. ⚠️
Neon’s branch system feels isolated, but it’s extremely easy to accidentally point both “test” and “prod” at the same branch endpoint.

Let me break it down precisely.

The Mistake: “Separate branches” but same endpoint
You think:

Prod = production branch
Test = test branch

But your app might actually be using:

DATABASE_URL=postgres://...@ep-cool-name-1234.us-east-2.aws.neon.tech/neondb
in both environments.

If that endpoint host is the same —
you’re hitting the same branch.

Why This Happens
Neon projects can have:

Multiple branches

Multiple roles

Multiple endpoints

Pooled vs Direct endpoints

Each branch has its own endpoint hostname.

Example:

Prod branch endpoint
ep-green-moon-12345.us-east-2.aws.neon.tech
Test branch endpoint
ep-silent-river-67890.us-east-2.aws.neon.tech
If your .env files both reference:

ep-green-moon-12345...
You are not separated.

The 3 Most Common Causes
1️⃣ Copy-paste mistake in .env
You created:

.env.production
.env.test
But both contain:

DATABASE_URL=postgres://...@ep-prod-host...
That’s it. Simple copy error.

2️⃣ Using pooled endpoint in one env, direct in another — but same branch
Neon gives:

Direct endpoint

Pooled endpoint (pgBouncer)

Example:

Prod:

ep-prod-host.neon.tech
Test:

ep-prod-host-pooler.neon.tech
These are STILL the same branch — just different connection modes.

Different hostname does NOT always mean different branch.

3️⃣ Your backend only loads one DATABASE_URL
In many Node apps:

process.env.DATABASE_URL
If:

Dev server loads .env

Production build loads .env.production

But your test server accidentally uses .env again…

You think you're testing, but you’re not.

How to Confirm If You’re Accidentally Pointing to Same Branch
Run this in BOTH environments:

SELECT current_database(),
       current_user,
       inet_server_addr(),
       inet_server_port();
If:

inet_server_addr() matches

inet_server_port() matches

You’re hitting the same endpoint.

Even more reliable:

In Neon Console:

Go to each branch

Look at Endpoint ID

Compare hostnames

They must be different.

The Subtle Risk (Why This Is Dangerous)
If test and prod point to same branch:

Running migrations in test = alters production schema

Deleting test data = deletes production data

Seed scripts contaminate prod

Feature testing changes real users’ data

This is how teams accidentally wipe prod.

How It Should Be Structured (Correct Setup)
In your project root:

.env.production
DATABASE_URL=postgres://...@ep-prod-branch-host...
.env.test
DATABASE_URL=postgres://...@ep-test-branch-host...
.env.local
DATABASE_URL=postgres://...@ep-dev-branch-host...
Each must point to a different Neon branch endpoint.

Extra Safe Pattern (I Recommend This)
Instead of:

DATABASE_URL=...
Use explicit names:

DATABASE_URL_PROD=...
DATABASE_URL_TEST=...
DATABASE_URL_DEV=...
Then in your app bootstrap:

const env = process.env.NODE_ENV;

const DATABASE_URL =
  env === "production"
    ? process.env.DATABASE_URL_PROD
    : env === "test"
    ? process.env.DATABASE_URL_TEST
    : process.env.DATABASE_URL_DEV;
Now you can’t accidentally cross-wire.

One More Important Neon-Specific Detail
Neon branches are lightweight and share underlying storage until changed.

So:

Even if schemas are identical,
you might think they’re the same.

But they’re isolated at the storage layer.

What matters is the endpoint hostname, not the schema similarity.

The Bottom Line
If your two environments:

Use the same endpoint hostname

Or same pooled host for same branch

Or same DATABASE_URL variable

Then your separation is fake.

If you paste:

Your .env.production

Your .env.test

The first 20 characters of each host (you can redact secrets)

I can instantly tell you if you’re safe or not.


give me the exactly code to run in the sql for each branch to detect the differences

You can’t run one SQL query that magically compares two branches at once (each branch is a separate database endpoint). But you can run the exact same SQL on each branch, copy the results, and diff them. ✅

Below are copy-paste queries you run in Neon SQL Editor on PROD branch and then on TEST branch.

0) Verify you’re truly on different endpoints (run first)
SELECT
  current_database()   AS db,
  current_user         AS user,
  inet_server_addr()   AS server_ip,
  inet_server_port()   AS server_port,
  version()            AS pg_version;
If server_ip + server_port are identical between branches, you’re likely not actually switching endpoints.

1) Extensions diff
SELECT extname, extversion
FROM pg_extension
ORDER BY extname;
2) Enums diff (VERY important for your app)
SELECT
  n.nspname AS schema,
  t.typname AS enum_name,
  e.enumsortorder,
  e.enumlabel AS enum_value
FROM pg_type t
JOIN pg_enum e ON e.enumtypid = t.oid
JOIN pg_namespace n ON n.oid = t.typnamespace
WHERE n.nspname IN ('public')
ORDER BY schema, enum_name, e.enumsortorder;
3) Tables present/missing diff
SELECT
  table_schema,
  table_name
FROM information_schema.tables
WHERE table_type = 'BASE TABLE'
  AND table_schema IN ('public')
ORDER BY table_schema, table_name;
4) Columns diff (type, nullability, default)
SELECT
  table_schema,
  table_name,
  ordinal_position,
  column_name,
  data_type,
  udt_name,
  is_nullable,
  column_default
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_schema IN ('public')
ORDER BY table_schema, table_name, ordinal_position;
5) Constraints diff (PK/FK/Unique/Checks)
SELECT
  conrelid::regclass::text AS table_name,
  conname                  AS constraint_name,
  contype                  AS constraint_type,  -- p=pk, f=fk, u=unique, c=check
  pg_get_constraintdef(oid) AS definition
FROM pg_constraint
WHERE connamespace = 'public'::regnamespace
ORDER BY table_name, constraint_name;
6) Indexes diff
SELECT
  schemaname,
  tablename,
  indexname,
  indexdef
FROM pg_indexes
WHERE schemaname = 'public'
ORDER BY tablename, indexname;
7) Triggers diff (often missed)
SELECT
  event_object_table AS table_name,
  trigger_name,
  action_timing,
  event_manipulation,
  action_statement
FROM information_schema.triggers
WHERE trigger_schema = 'public'
ORDER BY table_name, trigger_name, event_manipulation;
8) Views diff (if you use them)
SELECT table_schema, table_name
FROM information_schema.views
WHERE table_schema = 'public'
ORDER BY table_name;
Optional: One “fingerprint” query per branch (easy to compare)
This produces a single hash-like output for tables+columns+types+defaults in public.

SELECT md5(string_agg(row_text, '|' ORDER BY row_text)) AS schema_fingerprint
FROM (
  SELECT
    table_schema || '.' || table_name || '.' || column_name || ':' ||
    data_type || ':' || coalesce(udt_name,'') || ':' ||
    is_nullable || ':' || coalesce(column_default,'')
    AS row_text
  FROM information_schema.columns
  WHERE table_schema = 'public'
) x;
If the fingerprint differs, schema differs. (Then use queries 3–7 to see where.)

How to use this (exact workflow)
In Neon → open PROD branch → SQL Editor → run each query → copy results to a file prod.sql.out.

In Neon → open TEST branch → run same queries → copy results to test.sql.out.

Diff them with any tool (VS Code “Compare”, or diff).

If you want, paste the output of query #0 from both branches and I’ll tell you immediately if you’re even connected to different endpoints before you spend time diffing.

Base
production
Default
Latest available data (head)
Database
neondb
Compare
test
Latest available data (head)

Compare

--
-- Name: calc_job_charge_credits(uuid); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.calc_job_charge_credits(p_job_id uuid) RETURNS numeric
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$
DECLARE
  v_rate   numeric(12,2);
  v_hours  numeric(7,2);
  v_est    numeric(7,2);
  v_amount numeric(12,2);
BEGIN
  -- Lock row and load fields
  SELECT snapshot_total_rate_cph, actual_hours, estimated_hours
    INTO v_rate, v_hours, v_est
  FROM jobs
  WHERE id = p_job_id
  FOR UPDATE;

  -- Compute actual hours if missing
  IF v_hours IS NULL THEN
    PERFORM recompute_job_seconds(p_job_id);
    SELECT actual_hours INTO v_hours FROM jobs WHERE id = p_job_id;
  END IF;

  v_amount := ROUND(COALESCE(v_hours, v_est, 0) * COALESCE(v_rate, 0), 2);

  UPDATE jobs
  SET final_charge_credits = v_amount,
      updated_at = now()
  WHERE id = p_job_id;

  RETURN v_amount;
END;
$$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.calc_job_charge_credits(p_job_id uuid) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

--
-- Name: calc_job_charge_credits(public.cleaning_type, numeric, numeric, numeric, numeric); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.calc_job_charge_credits(cleaning public.cleaning_type, hours numeric, base_cph numeric, deep_cph numeric, moveout_cph numeric) RETURNS numeric
    LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE
    AS $$
DECLARE addon NUMERIC := 0;
BEGIN
  IF cleaning = 'deep' THEN
    addon := COALESCE(deep_cph,0);
  ELSIF cleaning = 'moveout' THEN
    addon := COALESCE(moveout_cph,0);
  END IF;
  RETURN (COALESCE(base_cph,0) + addon) * COALESCE(hours,0);
END; $$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.calc_job_charge_credits(cleaning public.cleaning_type, hours numeric, base_cph numeric, deep_cph numeric, moveout_cph numeric) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

--
-- Name: calculate_cancellation_fee_percent(numeric); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.calculate_cancellation_fee_percent(hours_before numeric) RETURNS numeric
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$
BEGIN
  IF hours_before > 48 THEN
    RETURN 0;    -- Free cancellation
  ELSIF hours_before > 24 THEN
    RETURN 50;   -- 50% fee
  ELSE
    RETURN 100;  -- 100% fee
  END IF;
END;
$$;

    AS $$
DECLARE
  deleted_count INTEGER;
BEGIN
  -- Clean up expired email verification tokens
  UPDATE users 
  SET email_verification_token = NULL,
      email_verification_token_expires_at = NULL
  WHERE email_verification_token_expires_at < NOW()
    AND email_verification_token IS NOT NULL;
  
  -- Clean up expired password reset tokens
  UPDATE users 
  SET password_reset_token = NULL,
      password_reset_token_expires_at = NULL
  WHERE password_reset_token_expires_at < NOW()
    AND password_reset_token IS NOT NULL;
  
  -- Clean up expired 2FA codes
  DELETE FROM two_factor_codes 
  WHERE expires_at < NOW();
  
  GET DIAGNOSTICS deleted_count = ROW_COUNT;
  
  -- Clean up expired sessions
  DELETE FROM user_sessions 
  WHERE expires_at < NOW();
  
  RETURN deleted_count;
END;
$$;


CREATE FUNCTION public.cleanup_old_idempotency_keys() RETURNS integer
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$
DECLARE
  deleted_count INTEGER;
BEGIN
  DELETE FROM idempotency_keys
  WHERE created_at < NOW() - INTERVAL '24 hours';
  
  GET DIAGNOSTICS deleted_count = ROW_COUNT;
  RETURN deleted_count;
END;
$$;

--
-- Name: gamification_use_reward(uuid); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.gamification_use_reward(grant_id uuid) RETURNS void
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$

BEGIN
  UPDATE gamification_reward_grants
  SET uses_remaining = CASE WHEN uses_remaining IS NULL THEN NULL WHEN uses_remaining <= 1 THEN 0 ELSE uses_remaining - 1 END,
      status = CASE WHEN uses_remaining IS NULL THEN status WHEN uses_remaining <= 1 THEN 'expired' ELSE status END
  WHERE id = grant_id AND status = 'active';



END;
$$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.gamification_use_reward(grant_id uuid) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

CREATE FUNCTION public.initialize_cleaner_level_progress() RETURNS trigger
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$
BEGIN
  IF NEW.role = 'cleaner' THEN
    INSERT INTO cleaner_level_progress (cleaner_id, current_level)
    VALUES (NEW.id, 1)
    ON CONFLICT (cleaner_id) DO NOTHING;
  END IF;
  RETURN NEW;
END;
$$;

-- Name: is_bank_holiday(date); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.is_bank_holiday(d date) RETURNS boolean
    LANGUAGE sql STABLE
    AS $$
  SELECT EXISTS (
    SELECT 1 FROM holidays h
    WHERE h.holiday_date = d AND h.bank_holiday = true
  );
$$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.is_bank_holiday(d date) OWNER TO neondb_owner;
DECLARE
  completed_at TIMESTAMPTZ;
BEGIN
  SELECT actual_end_at INTO completed_at
  FROM jobs
  WHERE id = p_job_id;
  
  IF completed_at IS NULL THEN
    RETURN true; -- Job not completed, always allow
  END IF;
  
  RETURN (NOW() - completed_at) <= INTERVAL '48 hours';
END;
$$;

    AS $$

  event_id UUID;
BEGIN
  INSERT INTO security_events (
    user_id,
    event_type,
    status,
    ip_address,

    metadata
  ) VALUES (
    p_user_id,
    p_event_type,

    p_ip_address,
    p_user_agent,
    p_metadata
  ) RETURNING id INTO event_id;
  
  RETURN event_id;
END;
$$;

--
-- Name: payout_initiate_date(date); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.payout_initiate_date(scheduled date) RETURNS date
    LANGUAGE plpgsql STABLE
    AS $$
BEGIN
  -- If scheduled is Sat/Sun, move back to Friday logic (defensive)
  IF EXTRACT(ISODOW FROM scheduled) IN (6,7) THEN
    scheduled := previous_business_day(scheduled + 1);
  END IF;

  -- If scheduled is a bank holiday, initiate previous business day (cleaner-friendly)
  IF is_bank_holiday(scheduled) THEN
    RETURN previous_business_day(scheduled);
  END IF;

  RETURN scheduled;
END;
$$;


CREATE FUNCTION public.previous_business_day(d date) RETURNS date
    LANGUAGE plpgsql STABLE
    AS $$
DECLARE
  x date := d - 1;
BEGIN
  WHILE (EXTRACT(ISODOW FROM x) IN (6,7)) OR is_bank_holiday(x) LOOP
    x := x - 1;
  END LOOP;

CREATE FUNCTION public.pt_haversine_meters(lat1 double precision, lon1 double precision, lat2 double precision, lon2 double precision) RETURNS double precision
    LANGUAGE sql IMMUTABLE
    AS $$



  SELECT 2 * 6371000 * asin(sqrt(pow(sin(radians((lat2 - lat1) / 2)), 2) + cos(radians(lat1)) * cos(radians(lat2)) * pow(sin(radians((lon2 - lon1) / 2)), 2)));


$$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.pt_haversine_meters(lat1 double precision, lon1 double precision, lat2 double precision, lon2 double precision) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

--
-- Name: recompute_job_seconds(text); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.recompute_job_seconds(job_id_in text) RETURNS bigint
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$
DECLARE total BIGINT;
BEGIN
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(segment_seconds),0)
    INTO total
  FROM job_time_logs
  WHERE job_id = job_id_in;

  UPDATE jobs
     SET total_seconds_worked = total
   WHERE id = job_id_in;

  RETURN total;
END; $$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.recompute_job_seconds(job_id_in text) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

--
-- Name: recompute_job_seconds(uuid); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.recompute_job_seconds(p_job_id uuid) RETURNS void
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$
DECLARE
  v_total_seconds INTEGER;
  v_hours NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  -- Recompute seconds for all closed segments of this job
  UPDATE job_time_logs
  SET seconds = GREATEST(
                  0,
                  EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM (segment_end - segment_start))::INTEGER
                )
  WHERE job_id = p_job_id
    AND segment_end IS NOT NULL;

  -- Sum seconds and convert to rounded hours (0.25h increments)
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(seconds), 0)
    INTO v_total_seconds
  FROM job_time_logs
  WHERE job_id = p_job_id
    AND seconds IS NOT NULL;

  v_hours := round_hours_15min(v_total_seconds);

  -- Persist on jobs
  UPDATE jobs
  SET actual_hours = v_hours,
      updated_at   = now()
  WHERE id = p_job_id;
END;
$$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.recompute_job_seconds(p_job_id uuid) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

-- Name: revoke_all_user_sessions(uuid); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.revoke_all_user_sessions(p_user_id uuid) RETURNS integer
    LANGUAGE plpgsql
    AS $$
DECLARE
  revoked_count INTEGER;
BEGIN
  UPDATE user_sessions 
  SET revoked = TRUE,
      revoked_at = NOW(),
      revoked_reason = 'user_logout_all'

  WHERE user_id = p_user_id
    AND NOT revoked;
  
  GET DIAGNOSTICS revoked_count = ROW_COUNT;
  
  RETURN revoked_count;
END;
$$;

--
-- Name: round_hours_15min(integer); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.round_hours_15min(seconds integer) RETURNS numeric
    LANGUAGE sql IMMUTABLE
    AS $$
  SELECT round((seconds::numeric / 3600.0) * 4) / 4;
$$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.round_hours_15min(seconds integer) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

--
-- Name: round_hours_15min(bigint, boolean); Type: FUNCTION; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE FUNCTION public.round_hours_15min(seconds bigint, round_up boolean DEFAULT false) RETURNS numeric
    LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE
    AS $$
DECLARE hrs NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  hrs := seconds / 3600.0;
  IF round_up THEN
    RETURN CEIL(hrs * 4)::NUMERIC / 4.0;
  ELSE
    RETURN ROUND(hrs * 4) / 4.0;
  END IF;
END; $$;


ALTER FUNCTION public.round_hours_15min(seconds bigint, round_up boolean) OWNER TO neondb_owner;

Yep — this diff output answers your earlier question ✅

Is it frontend data or backend data?
This is 100% backend (Postgres schema) 🧠⚙️
You’re looking at Neon’s Schema Diff between:

Base: production

Compare: test

So this is not UI state, not frontend cache, not React — it’s the actual database structure: schemas, enums, tables, functions, triggers, etc.

What the diff is telling you (the critical takeaway)
Your production and test branches are not aligned. In fact, they look like two different schema generations.

Here are the “red flags” I see immediately:

1) Multiple competing enum/type systems
You have duplicated concepts in multiple enums:

job_status and job_status_enum

payout_status and payout_status_enum

dispute_status and dispute_status_enum

cleaning_type (enum) vs earlier CleaningType expectation

user_role expanded in one place (super_admin/support/ops roles), but users table still checks role in a different way (customer/cleaner/admin check constraint)

That usually means migrations diverged and different code paths expect different types.

2) Two “users” models living at once
In your original reference you had:

users.id TEXT, email CITEXT, role user_role

But in this diff snippet you now show:

users.id uuid

users.role text

users_role_check constraint includes customer|cleaner|admin

Those are incompatible with the earlier “canonical” model you posted. That’s not cosmetic — that breaks code.

3) Entire subsystems exist in one branch but not the other
Your diff includes big platform features:

notifications schema (notifications)

admin settings + audit tables

background checks

cleaner AI settings/templates

availability blocks / blackout periods / time off

risk scoring, reliability events

cancellation policy tables

gamification tables

If production has these but test doesn’t (or vice versa), then “feature complete” is impossible until schema parity exists.

4) Broken/partial DDL in diff excerpt
I can see several enum definitions that are cut off in your pasted output:

Example:

CREATE TYPE public.cleaner_event_type AS ENUM ( … then nothing

same for client_risk_band, dispute_status, reschedule_bucket, etc.

That could be paste truncation or could indicate the schema dump/diff output got interrupted. If it’s real, that branch is not even valid.

Are we “done with everything we set out to do”?
No — not in the real-world sense.

We completed the planning and mapping work (data required for the interactive UI), but you cannot reliably implement until:

✅ Phase 0: Schema parity is achieved between test and production
Otherwise:

frontend will appear “randomly broken”

endpoints will fail in one env but not the other

types/enums won’t match

migrations won’t apply cleanly

What you should do next (tight, practical)
Step 1 — determine which branch is “truth”
Choose one:

Option A: Production is truth; test must match production.

Option B: Test is truth (newer); production needs migrations.

Given you called test “test db” and prod “production db”, safest is usually:
✅ Production = truth (unless you’re actively rebuilding prod)

Step 2 — check migration state in BOTH branches
Run this on each branch:

SELECT *
FROM schema_migrations
ORDER BY applied_at DESC NULLS LAST, migration_name ASC;
If the table doesn’t exist in one branch, that’s already proof the migration system differs.

Step 3 — schema fingerprint (fast compare)
Run on both branches:

SELECT md5(string_agg(row_text, '|' ORDER BY row_text)) AS schema_fingerprint
FROM (
  SELECT
    table_schema || '.' || table_name || '.' || column_name || ':' ||
    data_type || ':' || coalesce(udt_name,'') || ':' ||
    is_nullable || ':' || coalesce(column_default,'')
    AS row_text
  FROM information_schema.columns
  WHERE table_schema = 'public'
) x;
If different → schema mismatch confirmed (it will be).

If you want “Option A” (recommended): make TEST match PROD
Since you said “option a”, here’s what that means operationally:

✅ “production is canonical; test is a replica for safe testing”

Action: reset test branch to production state (Neon supports branch reset / recreate test from prod).
That’s much safer than trying to “incrementally patch” thousands of objects.

Then: apply new migrations forward from there.

Quick question you don’t need to answer (I’ll give both paths)
If you’re comfortable: tell me whether you want:

Path A (clean): recreate test from production
Best if you just want parity fast.

Path B (surgical): generate a patch script from diff
Best if you can’t recreate test.

If you reply with “A” or “B”, I’ll give you the exact step-by-step Neon workflow + exact SQL safety checks for that path.

    updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now() NOT NULL

--
-- Name: credit_summary_by_reason; Type: VIEW; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE VIEW public.credit_summary_by_reason AS
 SELECT reason,
    count(*) AS transaction_count,
    (sum(
        CASE
            WHEN (delta_credits > 0) THEN delta_credits
            ELSE 0
        END))::integer AS total_added,
    (sum(
        CASE
            WHEN (delta_credits < 0) THEN abs(delta_credits)
            ELSE 0
        END))::integer AS total_removed,
    (sum(delta_credits))::integer AS net_change
   FROM public.credit_ledger
  GROUP BY reason;


ALTER VIEW public.credit_summary_by_reason OWNER TO neondb_owner;

-- Name: jobs; Type: TABLE; Schema: public; Owner: neondb_owner
--

CREATE TABLE public.jobs (
    id uuid DEFAULT gen_random_uuid() NOT NULL,
    client_id uuid NOT NULL,
    cleaner_id uuid,
    status public.job_status DEFAULT 'created'::public.job_status NOT NULL,
    cleaning_type public.cleaning_type DEFAULT 'basic'::public.cleaning_type NOT NULL,
    estimated_hours numeric(5,2),
    actual_hours numeric(5,2),
    snapshot_total_rate_cph numeric(8,2),
    final_charge_credits numeric(10,2),
    created_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),
    updated_at timestamp with time zone DEFAULT now(),
    snapshot_base_rate_cph numeric(8,2),
    snapshot_addon_rate_cph numeric(8,2),
    escrow_credits_reserved numeric(12,2) DEFAULT 0 NOT NULL,
    refund_credits numeric(12,2),
    check_in_at timestamp with time zone,
    check_out_at timestamp with time zone,
    check_in_lat numeric(9,6),
    check_in_lng numeric(9,6),
    check_out_lat numeric(9,6),
    check_out_lng numeric(9,6),
    cleaner_notes text,
    tasks_completed_json jsonb,
    cancelled_at timestamp with time zone,
    scheduled_start_at timestamp with time zone,
    scheduled_end_at timestamp with time zone,
    actual_start_at timestamp with time zone,
    actual_end_at timestamp with time zone,
    estimated_minutes integer,
    actual_minutes integer,
    base_rate_cents bigint,
    extra_fees_cents bigint,
    discount_cents bigint,
    total_charge_cents bigint,
    credit_charge_credits numeric(12,2),
    title text,
    notes text,
    metadata jsonb,
    checkin_lat double precision,
    checkin_lng double precision,
    checkout_lat double precision,
    checkout_lng double precision,
    is_rush boolean DEFAULT false,
    rush_fee_credits integer DEFAULT 0,
    property_id integer,
    team_id integer,
    snapshot_is_holiday boolean DEFAULT false NOT NULL,
    snapshot_holiday_date date,
    snapshot_holiday_name text,
    snapshot_rate_multiplier numeric(6,3) DEFAULT 1.000 NOT NULL,
    has_addons boolean DEFAULT false,
    addons_count integer DEFAULT 0,
    address text NOT NULL,
    credit_amount integer DEFAULT 0 NOT NULL,
    latitude numeric(9,6),
    longitude numeric(9,6),
    rating integer,
    client_notes text
);


ALTER TABLE public.jobs OWNER TO neondb_owner;

CREATE TABLE public.referral_codes (
    id uuid DEFAULT gen_random_uuid() NOT NULL,
    user_id uuid NOT NULL,
    code text NOT NULL,
    type text DEFAULT 'standard'::text NOT NULL,
    reward_credits integer DEFAULT 20 NOT NULL,
    referee_credits integer DEFAULT 10 NOT NULL,
--

CREATE TABLE public.referrals (
    id uuid DEFAULT gen_random_uuid() NOT NULL,
    referrer_id uuid NOT NULL,
    referee_id uuid NOT NULL,
    referral_code text NOT NULL,
    status text DEFAULT 'pending'::text NOT NULL,
    referee_role text NOT NULL,
    jobs_required integer DEFAULT 3 NOT NULL,
 SELECT r.referrer_id,
    u.email,
    count(*) AS total_referrals,
    count(*) FILTER (WHERE (r.status = 'rewarded'::text)) AS successful_referrals,
    sum(r.referrer_reward) FILTER (WHERE (r.status = 'rewarded'::text)) AS total_credits_earned
   FROM (public.referrals r
     JOIN public.users u ON ((u.id = r.referrer_id)))
  GROUP BY r.referrer_id, u.email
  ORDER BY (count(*) FILTER (WHERE (r.status = 'rewarded'::text))) DESC;

    id uuid DEFAULT gen_random_uuid() NOT NULL,
    user_id uuid NOT NULL,
    token_jti text NOT NULL,
    device_info jsonb,

    country text,
    COALESCE(cfp.low_flexibility_active, false) AS low_flexibility_badge
   FROM ((public.users u
     JOIN public.cleaner_profiles cp ON ((cp.user_id = u.id)))
     LEFT JOIN public.cleaner_flex_profiles cfp ON ((cfp.cleaner_id = u.id)))
  WHERE ((u.role = 'cleaner'::text) AND (cp.is_available = true));

     LEFT JOIN public.client_risk_scores crs ON ((crs.client_id = u.id)))

You’ve got the bones of a pretty serious “trust-fintech” schema here 💳⚙️ — but the excerpt shows several structural hazards that will bite you in migrations, accounting integrity, and auditability.

Below is the highest-leverage cleanup pass (what’s wrong + what I’d do), based strictly on what you pasted.

1) Your DDL is syntactically incomplete in multiple places 🚨
Several CREATE TABLE blocks are missing:

the closing );

commas after the last column

sometimes entire column lists are cut off

ALTER TABLE ... OWNER appears before the table is fully defined in some places (in the snippet)

Examples from your paste:

credit_accounts ends with lifetime_spent integer DEFAULT 0 NOT NULL, -- and then stops.

credit_ledger ends with created_at ... NOT NULL then -- but no );

device_tokens ends mid-definition then immediately starts CREATE TABLE public.dispute_actions

many sequences (CREATE SEQUENCE ...) are cut without ;

✅ Fix approach: run the whole file through a formatter/parser before executing migrations (or enforce “one table per migration” so truncation can’t corrupt the file).

2) You currently have two competing “credit ledger” systems (pick one) ⚖️
You have:

public.credit_ledger (integer deltas, reason enum)

public.credit_transactions (numeric amount_credits, type enum, balance_after)

plus credit_accounts, credit_purchases, payment_intents (wallet_topup/job_charge)

and later: puretask.credit_transactions (another table with same name in another schema)

This is classic “double-entry drift”: different tables will disagree over time.

Recommended consolidation (cleanest):
Single source of truth: credit_ledger (append-only).

Every credit movement is a ledger entry.

Balance is derived (or maintained in credit_accounts via triggers/jobs).

Purchases, disputes, job charges, promos: all become ledger entries with references.

If you keep credit_transactions, then credit_ledger becomes redundant (or vice versa). Right now you’re maintaining both, which guarantees reconciliation pain.

3) Decide: are credits integers or decimals? (you mixed both) 🔢
credit_ledger.delta_credits integer

credit_accounts.current_balance integer

credit_transactions.amount_credits numeric(12,2)

jobs: final_charge_credits numeric(10,2) and credit_charge_credits numeric(12,2)

payouts: amount_credits numeric(10,2)

This matters a lot.

Best practice options:
Option A (recommended): credits are integers

1 credit = smallest unit (like cents)

Everything becomes integer or bigint

No rounding surprises

Option B: credits allow fractions

Then you must go all-in on numeric everywhere (numeric(12,2) or similar)

And enforce rounding rules consistently

Right now you’re half A / half B, which will cause mismatched balances and weird UI totals.

4) Identity confusion: user_id vs client_id vs cleaner_id 🧩
Some tables use:

user_id uuid

client_id uuid

cleaner_id uuid
…and FKs sometimes point to public.users(id) even when the semantic meaning is “client” or “cleaner”.

You also have both:

public.clients table (looks like profile-ish)

public.customers table (also profile-ish)

plus users role = client in some views

✅ Recommendation:

Use users(id) as the canonical identity.

Profile tables should be named client_profiles and cleaner_profiles (you already have cleaner_profiles elsewhere).

Prefer consistent FK names:

client_user_id uuid REFERENCES users(id)

cleaner_user_id uuid REFERENCES users(id)

If you keep clients as a table, don’t also keep customers unless they serve different business concepts.

5) Your constraints section shows multiple mismatched PRIMARY KEY / UNIQUE bindings 🧨
From your paste, there are lines like:

ALTER TABLE ONLY public.credit_accounts ADD CONSTRAINT credit_transactions_pkey PRIMARY KEY (id);
That’s almost certainly a naming/merge error (constraint name doesn’t match table).
Similar weirdness appears repeatedly.

✅ Recommendation:

Constraint names should match the table:

credit_accounts_pkey

credit_transactions_pkey

Enforce a naming convention and generate them deterministically.

6) Idempotency is good — but make it systematic ✅🔁
You already have:

credit_transactions.idempotency_key

unique partial index: credit_tx_idem_uniq

also a general idempotency_keys table

That’s great, but you want one standard:

Recommended pattern:
Every externally-triggered money/credits mutation must have:

idempotency_key text NOT NULL

unique index scoped properly:

either unique globally

or unique per endpoint/type

And the ledger should store it so duplicates never create double crediting.

7) Disputes + refunds: wire it directly into the credit system 💥
You have:

disputes.refund_amount_credits integer

dispute_actions audit log table (nice)

jobs have refund_credits numeric(12,2) and escrow_credits_reserved

✅ Best practice:

A dispute resolution should create a ledger entry (refund) referencing:

dispute_id

job_id

client_user_id

Never “set refund_amount_credits” and separately “adjust balances” without a ledger entry.

8) “Escrow credits reserved” needs invariants 🧱
Jobs show:

escrow_credits_reserved numeric(12,2) DEFAULT 0 NOT NULL

final_charge_credits numeric(10,2)

refund_credits numeric(12,2)

If you’re doing escrow, enforce:

escrow reserved ≥ final charge

refund ≤ final charge

escrow release happens exactly once

✅ Put those invariants either in:

constraints (limited but helpful)

or transaction logic + ledger entries + idempotency keys

9) Schema split: public vs puretask is currently messy 🗂️
You have duplicates like:

public.credit_transactions

puretask.credit_transactions

puretask.job_events plus public.job_events

If you’re doing multi-schema for namespacing, it must be consistent.

✅ Recommendation:

If this is a single app DB: use one schema (usually public) for application tables.

Use puretask only if you have a deliberate reason (multi-tenant separation, legacy boundary, etc.).

Avoid duplicate table names across schemas unless you really mean it.

The 5 changes I’d do first (highest ROI) 🚀
Pick one credits accounting source of truth (ledger-first).

Choose integer vs decimal credits and refactor all credit columns to match.

Unify identity keys (client_user_id, cleaner_user_id → users(id)).

Fix/normalize constraints naming + ensure every table has proper PK/FKs.

Make dispute resolutions and job charges write ledger entries with idempotency.

If you want: I can produce a clean “Credits v1” DDL (ledger + accounts + purchase + job charge + dispute refund) ✍️
To do it without guessing, I’ll assume this (based on your existing tables):

Postgres + Neon

public.users(id uuid) exists

Credits should probably be integer (simpler + safer)

If that assumption is wrong and you truly need fractional credits, I’ll adapt the DDL accordingly.

Yep — this error makes perfect sense once you zoom out a bit. Let’s break it down cleanly. ⚙️

Why you’re seeing this error
You’re currently inside Neon’s SQL Editor.

That editor only accepts PostgreSQL SQL statements.

But you pasted shell commands:

pg_dump "$PROD_URL" --schema-only > prod.sql
pg_dump "$TEST_URL" --schema-only > test.sql
diff prod.sql test.sql
Those are terminal / CLI commands, not SQL.

So Postgres is doing exactly what it should:

❌ “syntax error near pg_dump”

Because from Postgres’s point of view, pg_dump is just random text.

Important Concept (this is the key mental model)
There are two totally different environments:

✅ Neon SQL Editor
Runs:

SELECT

CREATE TABLE

ALTER

etc.

This talks to the database engine itself.

✅ Your local terminal / Cursor terminal / shell
Runs:

pg_dump

diff

psql

grep

These talk to Neon from outside.

You tried to run terminal tooling inside Postgres — that can’t work.

What you actually want to do
Since you’re using Cursor, do this locally.

Step 1 — Open Cursor terminal
In Cursor:

Ctrl + `
(or View → Terminal)

Step 2 — Set both connection strings
export PROD_URL="postgresql://..."
export TEST_URL="postgresql://..."
(use your real URLs)

Step 3 — Dump schemas
pg_dump "$PROD_URL" --schema-only > prod.sql
pg_dump "$TEST_URL" --schema-only > test.sql
This creates:

prod.sql

test.sql

in your project folder.

Step 4 — Diff them
On Mac/Linux:

diff prod.sql test.sql
On Windows (PowerShell):

Compare-Object (Get-Content prod.sql) (Get-Content test.sql)
or install Git Bash and use diff.

If you prefer PURE SQL (no pg_dump)
Since you’re already inside Neon UI, here’s the SQL-native way.

Run this in production branch:

SELECT table_schema, table_name, column_name, data_type
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_schema = 'public'
ORDER BY 1,2,3;
Export result as CSV.

Then switch to test branch and run the same.

Compare the CSVs.

That gives you:

✅ table differences
✅ column differences
✅ type differences

Why this matters for PureTask
Right now:

you have schema drift

multiple enum systems

duplicated credit systems

competing user models

Until prod + test match, everything else (animations, reliability UI, ledgers, maps) sits on shaky ground.

This is Phase Zero Infrastructure.

You’re doing the right thing by stopping here.

Ultra-clean Neon-native option (recommended)
Neon supports:

👉 Branch → Reset from production
This instantly makes test identical to prod.

is there a way to dump the whole db?

Yes — absolutely. And there are three real ways to dump the entire Neon database (schema + data). Which one you use depends on how much control you want and where you’re running it.

I’ll give you the clean, production-grade options.

✅ OPTION 1 — Full DB dump via pg_dump (recommended)
This gives you:

✔ schema
✔ data
✔ functions
✔ enums
✔ indexes
✔ constraints
✔ views

Run this in Cursor terminal (NOT Neon SQL editor):
pg_dump "$PROD_URL" > puretask_full_dump.sql
That’s it.

This creates:

puretask_full_dump.sql
in your current folder.

To compress:

pg_dump "$PROD_URL" | gzip > puretask_full_dump.sql.gz
Restore later if needed:
psql "$TEST_URL" < puretask_full_dump.sql
(or gunzip first if compressed)

✅ OPTION 2 — Custom format dump (best for large DBs)
This is what pros use:

pg_dump -Fc "$PROD_URL" > puretask.dump
Restore:

pg_restore -d "$TEST_URL" puretask.dump
Advantages:

✅ faster
✅ smaller
✅ selective restore
✅ parallel restore supported

✅ OPTION 3 — Neon UI Backup (easy button)
Inside Neon console:

Backup & Restore → Create backup
But:

⚠️ you don’t get a local file
⚠️ harder to diff
⚠️ harder to version

Use only for disaster recovery.

⚠️ IMPORTANT FOR PURETASK
Your DB is big and relationally complex:

credits

ledgers

jobs

disputes

payouts

gamification

AI settings

You should immediately adopt:

Nightly dump:
pg_dump -Fc "$PROD_URL" > backups/puretask_$(date +%F).dump
Store in:

S3

Backblaze

local encrypted drive

This is founder survival insurance.

🔥 Pro Tip (Elite Level)
Create two dumps:

Structure only:
pg_dump --schema-only "$PROD_URL" > schema.sql
Data only:
pg_dump --data-only "$PROD_URL" > data.sql
This lets you:

✅ diff schemas cleanly
✅ reload production structure without production data
✅ spin dev environments instantly

You want this:

pg_dump "$PROD_URL" > puretask_full.sql
Run in Cursor terminal.

NOT Neon SQL editor.
